					<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Interoception</span></h1>

	<input type="checkbox" id="p-lang-btn-checkbox" role="button" aria-haspopup="true" data-event-name="ui.dropdown-p-lang-btn" class="vector-dropdown-checkbox mw-interlanguage-selector" aria-label="Go to an article in another language. Available in 12 languages"   >

				<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body" aria-labelledby="firstHeading" data-mw-ve-target-container>
					<div class="vector-body-before-content">
							<div class="mw-indicators">
		</div>

						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-subjectpageheader">
</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Sensory system that receives and integrates information from the body</div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Interoception_and_the_body.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Interoception_and_the_body.png/500px-Interoception_and_the_body.png" decoding="async" width="462" height="300" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Interoception_and_the_body.png/960px-Interoception_and_the_body.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1498" data-file-height="972" /></a><figcaption>Interoception is involved in many different physiological systems like the cardiorespiratory system, gastrointestinal system, nociceptive system, endocrine and immune systems.</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Interoception</b> is the collection of <a href="/wiki/Sense#Other_internal_sensations_and_perceptions" title="Sense">senses</a> providing information to the organism about the internal state of the body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This can be both conscious and subconscious. It encompasses the brain's process of integrating signals relayed from the body into specific subregions—like the <a href="/wiki/Brainstem" title="Brainstem">brainstem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thalamus" title="Thalamus">thalamus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_somatosensory_cortex" title="Primary somatosensory cortex">somatosensory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">anterior cingulate cortex</a>—allowing for a complex and highly accurate representation of the physiological state of the body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This is important for maintaining <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostatic</a> conditions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:12&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in the body and, potentially, facilitating <a href="/wiki/Self-awareness" title="Self-awareness">self-awareness</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:10&#95;6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Interoceptive signals are projected to the brain via a diversity of <a href="/wiki/Neural_pathway" title="Neural pathway">neural pathways</a>, in particular from the lamina I of the spinal cord along the spinothalamic pathway and through the projections of the <a href="/wiki/Solitary_nucleus" title="Solitary nucleus">solitary nucleus</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that allow for the <a href="/wiki/Sensory_processing" title="Sensory processing">sensory processing</a> and prediction of internal bodily states. Misrepresentations of internal states, or a disconnect between the body's signals and the brain's interpretation and prediction of those signals, have been suggested to underlie conditions such as <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> depression, <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic disorder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anorexia_nervosa" title="Anorexia nervosa">anorexia nervosa</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Ambrosecchia&#95;Ardizzi&#95;Russo&#95;Ditaranto&#95;p.&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ambrosecchia_Ardizzi_Russo_Ditaranto_p.-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bulimia_nervosa" title="Bulimia nervosa">bulimia nervosa</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Klabunde&#95;Acheson&#95;Boutelle&#95;Matthews&#95;2013&#95;pp.&#95;488–492&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Klabunde_Acheson_Boutelle_Matthews_2013_pp._488–492-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">posttraumatic stress disorder</a> (PTSD), <a href="/wiki/Obsessive%E2%80%93compulsive_disorder" title="Obsessive–compulsive disorder">obsessive compulsive disorder</a> (OCD), <a href="/wiki/Attention_Deficit_Hyperactivity_Disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder">attention deficit hyperactivity disorder</a> (ADHD), <a href="/wiki/Alexithymia" title="Alexithymia">alexithymia</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Shah&#95;Hall&#95;Catmur&#95;Bird&#95;2016&#95;pp.&#95;215–220&#95;12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shah_Hall_Catmur_Bird_2016_pp._215–220-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Somatic_symptom_disorder" title="Somatic symptom disorder">somatic symptom disorder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Illness_anxiety_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Illness anxiety disorder">illness anxiety disorder</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Grossi&#95;Longarzo&#95;Quarantelli&#95;Salvatore&#95;2017&#95;pp.&#95;22–32&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grossi_Longarzo_Quarantelli_Salvatore_2017_pp._22–32-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The contemporary definition of interoception is not synonymous with the term "visceroception".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Visceroception refers to the perception of bodily signals arising specifically from the <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ (anatomy)">viscera</a>: the heart, lungs, stomach, and bladder, along with other internal organs in the trunk of the body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This does not include organs like the brain and skin. Interoception encompasses visceral signaling, but more broadly relates to all physiological tissues that relay a signal to the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a> about the current state of the body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:5&#95;16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Interoceptive signals are transmitted to the brain via multiple pathways including the <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">lamina I spinothalamic pathway</a>, the classical <a href="/wiki/General_visceral_afferent_fibers" class="mw-redirect" title="General visceral afferent fibers">viscerosensory pathway</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vagus_nerve" title="Vagus nerve">vagus nerve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glossopharyngeal_nerve" title="Glossopharyngeal nerve">glossopharyngeal nerve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemoreceptor" title="Chemoreceptor">chemosensory pathways</a> in the blood, and <a href="/wiki/Somatosensory_system" title="Somatosensory system">somatosensory pathways</a> from the skin.
</p><p>Interoceptive signals arise from many different physiological systems of the body. The most commonly studied system is <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiovascular">cardiovascular</a> interoception which is typically measured by directing attention towards the sensation of the heartbeat during various tasks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:7&#95;17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:6&#95;18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other physiological systems integral to interoceptive processing include the <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">respiratory system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gastrointestinal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genitourinary_system" title="Genitourinary system">genitourinary systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nociception" title="Nociception">nociceptive</a> system, <a href="/wiki/Thermoregulation" title="Thermoregulation">thermoregulatory</a> system, <a href="/wiki/Endocrine_system" title="Endocrine system">endocrine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">immune systems</a>. <a href="/wiki/Somatosensory_system#Neural_processing_of_social_touch" title="Somatosensory system">Soft cutaneous touch</a> is another sensory signal often included within the interoceptive processing system.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History_and_etymology">History and etymology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History and etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_to_mid-1900s">Early to mid-1900s</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early to mid-1900s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The concept of interoception was introduced in 1906 by the Nobel Laureate <a href="/wiki/Charles_Scott_Sherrington" title="Charles Scott Sherrington">Sir Charles S. Sherrington</a>. He did not use the noun <i>interoception</i>, but did describe as <i>interoceptive</i><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> those receptors that are within the viscera—what are today called "visceroceptive"—and thus excluded all other receptors and information from the body, which he grouped as either <i>exteroceptive</i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Proprioception" title="Proprioception">proprioceptive</a></i>. In Sherrington's model, exteroceptive receptors were those that received information from outward stimuli, like light, touch, sound, and odor. He classified <a href="/wiki/Thermoception" title="Thermoception">temperature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nociception" title="Nociception">nociception</a> as exteroceptive sensations as well, though these are now regarded as having interoceptive qualities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:5&#95;16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He further divided the internal milieu of the body by its <a href="/wiki/Somatic_nervous_system" title="Somatic nervous system">somatic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autonomic_nervous_system" title="Autonomic nervous system">autonomic</a> functions. And proprioceptors were those found in <a href="/wiki/Skeletal_muscle" title="Skeletal muscle">skeletal tissue</a> that control voluntary movement. For him, <a href="/wiki/Interoceptor" class="mw-redirect" title="Interoceptor">interoceptors</a> (a term which has lost prevalence in modern literature) were thus confined to visceral involuntary <a href="/wiki/Smooth_muscle_tissue" class="mw-redirect" title="Smooth muscle tissue">smooth muscle</a> (e.g. surrounding blood vessels).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Further work on interoceptive processing after Sherrington was delayed for many years owing to the influential claim by <a href="/wiki/John_Newport_Langley" title="John Newport Langley">John Newport Langley</a> that the <a href="/wiki/Autonomic_nervous_system" title="Autonomic nervous system">autonomic nervous system</a> used only <a href="/wiki/Efferent_nerve_fiber" title="Efferent nerve fiber">efferent</a> (brain-to-body) signaling to implement its functions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
By the 1950s and 1960s, many investigations of interoceptive processing had been conducted, and once it had become apparent that interoceptive receptors are present in many tissues of the body other researchers began to investigate afferent body-to-brain signals, mainly by conducting animal experiments to see if interoceptive conditioning was possible. Using principles of <a href="/wiki/Classical_conditioning" title="Classical conditioning">Pavlovian conditioning</a>, different physiological systems in dogs were perturbed to elicit a conditioned response to food.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For example, in one experiment, <a href="/wiki/Dogs" class="mw-redirect" title="Dogs">dogs</a>' pelvises were distended using infusions of solution when food was presented to them. After rounds of pairing the two, salivation occurred without presenting food once the <a href="/wiki/Pelvis" title="Pelvis">pelvis</a> was distended.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Interoceptive conditioning studies like this illustrated that interoceptive sensations may be important for learned behavior and emotion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mid-1900s_to_2000">Mid-1900s to 2000</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mid-1900s to 2000"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_articles_referencing_interoception_from_1905_to_2015.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Number_of_articles_referencing_interoception_from_1905_to_2015.png/500px-Number_of_articles_referencing_interoception_from_1905_to_2015.png" decoding="async" width="450" height="278" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3b/Number_of_articles_referencing_interoception_from_1905_to_2015.png 1.5x" data-file-width="611" data-file-height="377" /></a><figcaption>This graph shows the number of articles that reference the term "interoception" specifically from 1905 to 2015. A clear increase in the number of publications per year on the topic is seen in the 21st century.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The increased interest in interoception during the late 1950s and the 1960s, as evidenced by the number of papers published, has been referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Biofeedback" title="Biofeedback">biofeedback</a> blip". This was a phase during which many researchers examined humans' ability to gain control over <a href="/wiki/Autonomic_nervous_system" title="Autonomic nervous system">autonomic</a> functions as a method of treatment for various conditions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Interoception did not gain widespread popularity within the scientific community until the mid- to late-twentieth century. During that period, some researchers chose to use the terms <i>visceroceptor</i> and <i>interoceptor</i> interchangeably, in line with Sherrington's usage,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> others combined proprioceptive and visceroceptive information into one category—interoception—based on physiological data about the lack of differences in <a href="/wiki/Nerve_impulses" class="mw-redirect" title="Nerve impulses">nerve impulses</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and still others proposed that interoception includes more than just <a href="/wiki/Endogeny_(biology)" title="Endogeny (biology)">endogenous</a> (internal) stimuli.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:2&#95;14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Exactly which sensory signals could or should be classified as interoceptive remains the subject of ongoing debate.
</p><p>During the 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Psychophysiology" title="Psychophysiology">psychophysiologists</a> began to extensively examine cardiovascular interoception, introducing several different experimental tasks for studying the perception of the heartbeat: heartbeat counting,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:7&#95;17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> heartbeat tapping,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:8&#95;26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and heartbeat detection.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">Psychiatrists</a> also began to look at the effects of pharmacological stimulation on the symptoms of <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic disorder</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All of this further increased researchers' interest in interoception, including the development of theoretical models of the integration of interoceptive information within the body over time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2000_and_on">2000 and on</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2000 and on"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The twenty-first century has seen a tremendous increase in publications on the topic of interoception, and to a recognition of its multifaceted nature.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This has led to the emergence of different ideas about interoception. One contemporary definition widens the concept to encompass "the skin and all that is underneath the skin" and the perception and function of bodily activity<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to more fully understand psychosomatic processes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:5&#95;16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In a similar vein, <a href="/wiki/Neuroanatomy" title="Neuroanatomy">neuroanatomists</a> hoping to find the anatomical basis of interoceptive functioning have stated the existence of a <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostatic</a> pathway from the body to the brain that represents "the physiological status of all tissues in the body," and that this mapping onto the brain provides an individual with subjective feeling states that are critical for human <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Self-awareness" title="Self-awareness">self-awareness</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For example, interoception is the fundament of the modern view on <a href="/wiki/Allostasis" title="Allostasis">allostasis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allostatic_load" title="Allostatic load">allostatic load</a>. The regulatory model of allostasis claims that the brain's primary role as an organ is the predictive regulation of internal sensations. <a href="/wiki/Predictive_homeostasis" class="mw-redirect" title="Predictive homeostasis">Predictive regulation</a> is the brain's ability to anticipate needs and prepare to fulfill them before they arise.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In this model, the brain is responsible for efficient regulation of its internal milieu.
</p><p>Interoception is sometimes generally referred to as "the perception of internal body states"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:6&#95;18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although there are many interoceptive processes that are not consciously perceived. Importantly, interoception is made possible through a process of "integrating the information coming from inside the body into the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This definition deviates from Sherrington's original proposition, but exemplifies the dynamic and widening breadth of interoception as a concept in modern literature.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Facets_of_interoception">Facets of interoception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Facets of interoception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left: 10px; width: 50%">
<caption>Different facets or components of interoception
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Facet</th>
<th>Operational definition
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Attention</td>
<td>Observing internal body sensations
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Detection</td>
<td>Presence or absence of conscious report
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Magnitude</td>
<td>Intensity
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Discrimination</td>
<td>Localize sensation to a specific channel or organ system, and differentiate it from other sensations
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Accuracy (or sensitivity)</td>
<td>Correct and precise monitoring
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Self-Report</td>
<td>Reflect upon one's own experiences of interoceptive states, make judgements about their outcomes, and describe them through verbal or motor responses
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Although interoception as a term has more recently gained increased popularity, different aspects of it have been studied since the 1950s. These include the features of attention, detection, magnitude, discrimination, accuracy, sensibility, and self-reporting.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Despite not using the word <i>interoception</i> specifically, many publications in the <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiology</a> and medical fields have focused on understanding interoceptive information processing in different <a href="/wiki/Organ_systems" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ systems">organ systems</a>. Attention describes the ability to observe sensations within the body, it can be directed voluntarily in a "<a href="/wiki/Top-down_and_bottom-up_design" class="mw-redirect" title="Top-down and bottom-up design">top down</a>" manner or it can be attracted involuntarily in a "bottom up" manner.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Detection reflects the presence or absence of a conscious report of interoceptive stimuli, like a heartbeat or growling stomach. Magnitude is the intensity of the stimulus, or how strongly the stimuli is felt. Discrimination describes the ability to localize interoceptive stimuli in the body to specific organs and differentiate them from other bodily stimuli that also occur, like distinguishing between a heart which is beating hard from an upset stomach. Accuracy (or sensitivity) refers to how precisely and correctly an individual can monitor specific interoceptive processes.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Self-reporting is itself multifaceted. It describes the ability to reflect on interoceptive experiences occurring over different periods of time, make judgments about them, and describe them. <a href="/wiki/Brain-body_interaction" class="mw-redirect" title="Brain-body interaction">Brain-body interactions</a> can also be studied using neuroimaging techniques to map functional interactions between brain and peripheral signals. Although all of these components of interoception have been studied since the mid-twentieth century, they have not been brought together under the umbrella term "interoception" until more recently.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>
The term "interoceptive awareness" is also frequently used to encompass any (or all) of the different interoception features that are accessible to conscious self-report. This multifaceted approach offers a unified way of looking at interoceptive functioning and its different features, it clarifies the definition of interoception itself, and it informs structured ways of assessing interoceptive experiences in an individual.</p><figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Facets_of_interoception.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Facets_of_interoception.png/500px-Facets_of_interoception.png" decoding="async" width="472" height="315" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Facets_of_interoception.png 1.5x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="394" /></a><figcaption>This graph shows the number of articles published on interoception vs. articles published on interoceptive facets without directly referencing the term from 1905 to 2015. The timeline starts one year before the publication of Charles Sherrington's book, <i>The integrative action of the nervous system</i>, which introduced "interoception".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Interoceptive_physiology">Interoceptive physiology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Interoceptive physiology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
