<td>Khalsa ‎<br />2009
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Cardiac interoception has been widely studied as a method of evaluating interoceptive sensation. This is done using different tasks including heartbeat counting,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:7&#95;17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> heartbeat tapping,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:8&#95;26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> heartbeat detection<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and heartbeat attention<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:9&#95;36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:19&#95;37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:19-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> tasks. Heartbeat counting tasks ask participants to count the number of felt heartbeats during short time periods. Their reported count is then compared with the actual count obtained with an <a href="/wiki/Electrocardiography" title="Electrocardiography">electrocardiogram</a>. This measures the participant's attention to his or her own heartbeat, the accuracy with which that is perceived, and the ability of the participant to report that measurement. However, results can be influenced by the participant's preexisting knowledge of his or her heart rate<sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and an insensitivity to <a href="/wiki/Heart_rate" title="Heart rate">heart rate</a> change.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Heartbeat detection tasks work by providing a participant with a musical tone which is played simultaneously or non-simultaneously with one's heartbeat, asking the participant to report whether it is simultaneous or not with the tones. Heartbeat detection is commonly used because of its ability discern an individual's performance above chance levels, so-called "good detectors". However, such detection rates among participants for this task are usually only 35%.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also measures the participant's attention, detection, discrimination, accuracy and self-report of the interoceptive process.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Heartbeat attention tasks are the most minimalistic, and involve simply the top-down direction of attention towards an interoceptive sensation such as the heartbeat, breath, or stomach.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:9&#95;36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most perceptions of heartbeat sensations usually occur during a time of homeostatic perturbation, such as when the state of the body changes from external or internal influences such as physical exertion or elevated arousal states, e.g., riding a roller coaster, watching a scary movie, public speaking anxiety, or having a panic attack. For this reason, cardiac interoception is also sometimes studied by inducing perturbations of bodily state. This can be done pharmacologically using <a href="/wiki/Adrenaline" title="Adrenaline">adrenaline</a>-like drugs, such as <a href="/wiki/Isoproterenol" class="mw-redirect" title="Isoproterenol">isoproterenol</a>, which mimic activation of the <a href="/wiki/Sympathetic_nervous_system" title="Sympathetic nervous system">sympathetic nervous system</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:6&#95;18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> resulting in increased heart rate and respiration rate, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Fight-or-flight_response" title="Fight-or-flight response">"fight-or-flight" response</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This approach provides a physiological basis for understanding <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">psychiatric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neurological_disorder" title="Neurological disorder">neurological disorders</a> that are characterized by heightened <a href="/wiki/Sympathetic_nervous_system" title="Sympathetic nervous system">sympathetic nervous system</a> activity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:6&#95;18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Respiratory_and_chemoreceptive_system">Respiratory and chemoreceptive system</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Respiratory and chemoreceptive system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Respiratory perception can differ from other interoceptive physiological symptoms because of an individual's ability to exert voluntary control over the system with <a href="/wiki/Control_of_ventilation#Voluntary_control_of_respiration" title="Control of ventilation">controlled breathing</a> or breathing exercises.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:4&#95;4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This system is often measured using restrictive breathing loads<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and/or <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1123817410">.mw-parser-output .template-chem2-su{display:inline-block;font-size:80%;line-height:1;vertical-align:-0.35em}.mw-parser-output .template-chem2-su>span{display:block;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output sub.template-chem2-sub{font-size:80%;vertical-align:-0.35em}.mw-parser-output sup.template-chem2-sup{font-size:80%;vertical-align:0.65em}</style><span class="chemf nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">CO<sub class="template-chem2-sub">2</sub></a></span> inhalation,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which are designed to mimic <a href="/wiki/Labored_breathing" title="Labored breathing">labored breathing</a> sensations. <a href="/wiki/Dyspnea" class="mw-redirect" title="Dyspnea">Dyspnea</a>, or difficulty breathing, is a commonly felt sensation associated with panic attacks; however, due to the voluntary control of breathing, this domain of interoception usually requires implementation of much more elaborate experimental controls to quantify in comparison to cardiac interoception.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Gastrointestinal_and_genitourinary_systems">Gastrointestinal and genitourinary systems</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Gastrointestinal and genitourinary systems"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Hunger_(motivational_state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hunger (motivational state)">Hunger (motivational state)</a></div>
<p>Common interoceptive sensations related to the gastrointestinal and genitourinary systems are hunger and fullness. These are <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostatic</a> signals that tell an individual when to eat and when to stop eating. The dorsal mid-insula appears to be integral in taste processing during gastrointestinal interoceptive attention tasks.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Rectal and bladder distensions are used as a method to perturb the homeostatic environment of the <a href="/wiki/Gastrointestinal_tract" title="Gastrointestinal tract">gastrointestinal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Genitourinary_system" title="Genitourinary system">genitourinary</a> systems, using placement of <a href="/wiki/Balloon_catheter" title="Balloon catheter">balloon catheters</a> which can be inflated to achieve different stimulus intensities. <a href="/wiki/Learning#Associative_learning" title="Learning">Associative fear learning</a> paradigms have been used to study how innocuous signals might lead to abnormal states of gastrointestinal hypersensitivity and <a href="/wiki/Anxiety" title="Anxiety">anxiety</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Biofeedback" title="Biofeedback">Biofeedback</a> therapy has been used for individuals with impaired gastrointestinal interoception, showing positive outcomes for some patients.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Nociceptive_system">Nociceptive system</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Nociceptive system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nociception" title="Nociception">Nociception</a> refers to the receiving and processing of pain inducing stimuli by the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a>. Functional brain imaging studies during painful stimulation of the skin with heated probes, during mechanical compression, and electric shock have suggested that the <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insular cortex</a> is prominently activated during pain processing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:13&#95;48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thus while pain was once thought of as an exteroceptive sensation, based on functional imaging and anatomical evidence it is now understood that it has an interoceptive component.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Thermoregulatory_system">Thermoregulatory system</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Thermoregulatory system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Temperature and pain are thought to be represented as "feelings" of coolness and warmness and pleasantness or unpleasantness in the brain. These sensory and affective characteristics of <a href="/wiki/Thermoregulation" title="Thermoregulation">thermoregulation</a> may motivate certain behavioral responses depending on the state of the body (for example, moving away from a source of heat to a cooler space). Such perturbations in the internal <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">homeostatic</a> environment of an organism are thought to be key aspects of a motivational process giving rise to <a href="/wiki/Homeostatic_emotion" class="mw-redirect" title="Homeostatic emotion">emotional states</a>, and have been proposed to be represented principally by the <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insular cortex</a> as feelings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:10&#95;6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These feelings then influence drives when the <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">anterior cingulate cortex</a> is activated.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Endocrine_and_immune_systems">Endocrine and immune systems</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Endocrine and immune systems"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Endocrine_system" title="Endocrine system">endocrine</a> and immune systems are necessary body systems that aid in allostasis and homeostatic control. Imbalances in these systems, along with other genetic and social factors, may be linked to interoceptive dysregulation in depression.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These increased allostatic changes may cause a hyperawareness of interoceptive signaling and a hypo-awareness of exteroceptive signaling in depression patients.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Affective_touch">Affective touch</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Affective touch"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Somatosensory_system#Neural_processing_of_social_touch" title="Somatosensory system">Neural processing of social touch</a></div>
<p>Affective touch refers to the stimulation of slow, unmyelinated <a href="/wiki/C_tactile_afferent" title="C tactile afferent">C tactile afferents</a>. This is accompanied by a sense of pleasantness, and has been linked to brain–heart interactions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>, and likened to other interoceptive modalities like thermoregulation and nociception because of the similarities in anatomical function.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:11&#95;52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Soft touch activates the <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insula</a> rather than the <a href="/wiki/Primary_somatosensory_cortex" title="Primary somatosensory cortex">somatosensory cortex</a>, indicating that it has an affective importance absent in <a href="/wiki/Type_II_sensory_fiber" title="Type II sensory fiber">Aβ fibers</a>. Since soft touch utilizes a separate pathway, it may have a social relevancy, allowing the body to separate the "noise" of outward stimuli from stimuli that evokes an affective feeling.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:11&#95;52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Neuroanatomical_pathways">Neuroanatomical pathways</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Neuroanatomical pathways"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Multiple neural pathways relay information integral to interoceptive processing from the body to the brain. these include the lamina I <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">spinothalamic pathway</a>, the visceroceptive pathway, and the <a href="/wiki/Somatosensory_system" title="Somatosensory system">somatosensory pathway</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Lamina_I_spinothalamic_pathway">Lamina I spinothalamic pathway</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Lamina I spinothalamic pathway"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The lamina I spinothalamic pathway is commonly known for carrying information to the brain about temperature and pain, but it has been suggested to more broadly relay all information about the homeostatic condition of the body.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:13&#95;48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Afferent signals enter the spinal cord at the superficial layer of the <a href="/wiki/Posterior_grey_column" class="mw-redirect" title="Posterior grey column">dorsal horn</a></li>
<li>Second order neurons cross the midline of the <a href="/wiki/Spinal_cord" title="Spinal cord">spinal cord</a> and project up the opposite side, synapsing on the <a href="/wiki/Solitary_nucleus" title="Solitary nucleus">nucleus of the solitary tract</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parabrachial_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Parabrachial area">parabrachial nucleus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Periaqueductal_gray" title="Periaqueductal gray">periaqueductal gray</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Brainstem" title="Brainstem">brainstem</a></li>
<li>Third order neurons in the <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posteromedial_nucleus" title="Ventral posteromedial nucleus">ventral posteromedial nucleus</a> in the thalamus relay the signal to the dorsal posterior <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insula</a></li>
<li>The signal is re-represented on either the right or left side</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Visceroceptive_pathway">Visceroceptive pathway</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Visceroceptive pathway"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The visceroceptive pathway relays information about visceral organs to the brain.
</p>
<ul><li>Afferent signals from the <a href="/wiki/Vagus_nerve" title="Vagus nerve">vagus nerve</a> enter the <a href="/wiki/Brainstem" title="Brainstem">brainstem</a> making synaptic connections with the <a href="/wiki/Solitary_nucleus" title="Solitary nucleus">nucleus of the solitary tract</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parabrachial_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Parabrachial area">parabrachial nucleus</a></li>
<li>The signal is relayed to the <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posteromedial_nucleus" title="Ventral posteromedial nucleus">ventromedial basal nucleus</a> of the thalamus</li>
<li>Third order neurons send the signal to the posterior <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insula</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Somatosensory_pathway">Somatosensory pathway</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Somatosensory pathway"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Somatosensory_system" title="Somatosensory system">Somatosensory system</a></div>
<p>The somatosensory pathway relays information about proprioception and <a href="/wiki/Fine_touch" class="mw-redirect" title="Fine touch">discriminative touch</a> to the brain through different receptors in the skin.
</p>
<ul><li>Afferent signals from the <a href="/wiki/Mechanoreceptor" title="Mechanoreceptor">mechanoreceptors</a> or proprioceptors enter the spinal cord at the dorsal root ganglia</li>
<li>Second order neurons cross the midline in the medulla, projecting up the opposite side and synapse on third order neurons in the <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posterolateral_nucleus" title="Ventral posterolateral nucleus">ventral posterior lateral nucleus</a> or ventromedial posterior nucleus of the thalamus</li>
<li>Third order neurons in the thalamus relay the signal to the <a href="/wiki/Primary_somatosensory_cortex" title="Primary somatosensory cortex">primary somatosensory cortex</a> in the brain<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="there is no reason to talk about tactile and proprioceptive pathways as they are anatomically separate from the interoceptive one (August 2021)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Cortical_processing_of_interoception">Cortical processing of interoception</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cortical processing of interoception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Thalamus">Thalamus</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Thalamus"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The thalamus receives signals from sympathetic and parasympathetic afferents during interoceptive processing. The <a href="/wiki/Ventral_posteromedial_nucleus" title="Ventral posteromedial nucleus">ventromedial posterior nucleus</a> (VMpo) is a subregion of the thalamus which receives sympathetic information from lamina I <a href="/wiki/Spinothalamic_tract" title="Spinothalamic tract">spinothalamic neurons</a>. The human VMpo is much larger than that of primates and sub-primates<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is important for processing of nociceptive, thermoregulatory, and visceral sensations. The <a href="/wiki/Ventrobasal_complex" title="Ventrobasal complex">ventromedial basal nucleus</a> (VMb) receives parasympathetic information from <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ (anatomy)">visceral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taste" title="Taste">gustatory systems</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Insular_cortex">Insular cortex</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Insular cortex"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">Insular cortex</a></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Insula_structure.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Insula_structure.png/500px-Insula_structure.png" decoding="async" width="460" height="258" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Insula_structure.png 1.5x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="364" /></a><figcaption>This image divides the insula into its anterior, mid, and posterior regions, with each being denoted by different colors</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">insula</a> is critically involved in the processing, integration, and cortical representation of visceral and interoceptive information. Lamina I spinothalamic and vagal afferents project via the brainstem and thalamus to the posterior and mid dorsal insula respectively. From there, information travels to the posterior and mid-insula, which combines visceral and somatosensory information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:9&#95;36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The insula is also activated during a variety of exteroceptive and affective tasks. The insula is considered to be a "hub" region because it has an extremely high number of connections with other brain areas, suggesting it may be important for an integration of lower-level physiological information and <a href="/wiki/Salience_(neuroscience)" title="Salience (neuroscience)">salience</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_insula_and_connecting_brain_regions.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/The_insula_and_connecting_brain_regions.png/500px-The_insula_and_connecting_brain_regions.png" decoding="async" width="461" height="271" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/The_insula_and_connecting_brain_regions.png/960px-The_insula_and_connecting_brain_regions.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1696" data-file-height="996" /></a><figcaption>The insula connects to many regions in the brain and is highly involved in many homeostatic functions.</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Anterior_insular_cortex">Anterior insular cortex</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Anterior insular cortex"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The anterior insular cortex (AIC) is involved in the representation of "cognitive feelings" which arise from the moment-to-moment integration of homeostatic information from the body. These feelings engender self-awareness by creating a sentient being (someone able to feel and perceive) aware of bodily and cognitive processing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:13&#95;48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Essentially all subjective bodily feelings are associated with activation in the anterior insula: interoceptive feelings come to awareness in the anterior insula.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-olausson&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olausson-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-kong&#95;57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kong-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-small&#95;58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-small-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>PET studies of cool feelings revealed that activiation that correlated with the subjective ratings of cool temperatures on the hand appeared first in the mid-insula, and then it was strongest in the right anterior insula and <a href="/wiki/Orbitofrontal_cortex" title="Orbitofrontal cortex">orbitofrontal cortex</a>. Feelings from the body of heat pain or C-tactile affective touch also produce activation in the posterior, mid-, and anterior insula, and the strongest activation associated with these subjective feelings is in the anterior insula.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-olausson&#95;56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olausson-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-kong&#95;57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kong-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-small&#95;58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-small-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>One study of heat pain explicitly showed that activation in the dorsal posterior insula correlated with objective painful heat intensity, whereas activation in the right anterior insula correlated with subjective pain intensity ratings. Similarly, subjective ratings of flavors and tastes correlates strongly with activation in the left anterior insula. The available evidence supports the interpretation that feelings from the body is engendered in the anterior insula.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-olausson&#95;56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olausson-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-kong&#95;57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kong-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-small&#95;58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-small-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cytoarchitecture_and_granulation">Cytoarchitecture and granulation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cytoarchitecture and granulation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cytoarchitecture" title="Cytoarchitecture">Insular cortex cytoarchitecture</a></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Insular_cortex_granulation.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Insular_cortex_granulation.png/500px-Insular_cortex_granulation.png" decoding="async" width="461" height="254" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/Insular_cortex_granulation.png 1.5x" data-file-width="726" data-file-height="400" /></a><figcaption>The insular cortex differs cytoarchitecturally based on its anterior, mid, and posterior regions. The posterior insular cortex is granular, the mid insular cortex is dysgranular (or slightly granulated) and the anterior insular cortex has no granulation whatsoever.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The insula contains three major subregions defined by the presence or absence of a <a href="/wiki/Granule_cell" title="Granule cell">granule cell</a> layer: <a href="/wiki/Granular_insular_cortex" title="Granular insular cortex">granular</a>, dysgranular (slightly granulated) <a href="/wiki/Agranular_insula" title="Agranular insula">agranular</a>. Each of these portions of the insular cortex are important for different levels of functional connectivity. Information from the thalamus is projected to all three regions. Those with increased granulation are considered to be capable of receiving sensory input.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:12&#95;5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Anterior_cingulate_cortex">Anterior cingulate cortex</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Anterior cingulate cortex"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">anterior cingulate cortex</a> (ACC) plays a significant role in <a href="/wiki/Motivation" title="Motivation">motivation</a> and the creation of <a href="/wiki/Emotion" title="Emotion">emotion</a>. An emotion can be seen as comprising both a feeling and a motivation based on that feeling. According to one view, the "feeling" is represented in the insula, while the "motivation" is represented in the ACC.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:1&#95;3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many interoceptive tasks activate the insula and ACC together, specifically tasks that elicit strong aversive feeling states like pain.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Somatosensory_cortex">Somatosensory cortex</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Somatosensory cortex"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Primary_somatosensory_cortex" title="Primary somatosensory cortex">sensory motor cortex</a> provides an alternative pathway for sensing interoceptive stimuli. Although not following the conventional pathway for <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex#Interoceptive_awareness" title="Insular cortex">interoceptive awareness</a>, skin afferents which project to the primary and secondary somatosensory cortices provide the brain with information regarding bodily information. This area of the brain is commonly engaged by gastrointestinal distension and nociceptive stimulation, but it likely plays a role in representing other interoceptive sensations as well.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:14&#95;60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In one study, a patient with bilateral insula and <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">ACC</a> damage was given <a href="/wiki/Isoprenaline" title="Isoprenaline">isoproterenol</a> as a method of exciting the <a href="/wiki/Circulatory_system#Cardiovascular_system" title="Circulatory system">cardiovascular system</a>. Despite damage to putative interoceptive areas of the brain, the patient was able to perceive his heartbeat with similar accuracy compared to healthy individuals; however, once <a href="/wiki/Lidocaine" title="Lidocaine">lidocaine</a> was applied to the patient's chest over the region of maximum cardiac sensation and the test was run again, the patient did not sense any change in heartbeat whatsoever.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:14&#95;60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This suggested that somatosensory information from afferents innervating the skin outside of the heart may provide information to the brain about the heart's pounding through the somatosensory cortex.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:14&#95;60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Interoception_and_emotion">Interoception and emotion</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Interoception and emotion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Homeostatic_emotion" class="mw-redirect" title="Homeostatic emotion">Homeostatic emotion</a></div>
<p>The relationship between interoception and emotional experience is an intimate one. In the late 19th century, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> noted and discussed the involvement of sensations from the <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ (anatomy)">viscera</a> by describing similarities between humans and animals reactions to fear in his book, <a href="/wiki/The_Expression_of_the_Emotions_in_Man_and_Animals" title="The Expression of the Emotions in Man and Animals"><i>The Expression of Emotions in Man and Animals</i></a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:6&#95;18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later, <a href="/wiki/William_James" title="William James">William James</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Lange_(physician)" title="Carl Lange (physician)">Carl Lange</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/James%E2%80%93Lange_theory" title="James–Lange theory">James-Lange theory of emotion</a>, which states that bodily sensations provide the critical basis for emotional experience.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:15&#95;61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:15-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Somatic_marker_hypothesis" title="Somatic marker hypothesis">somatic marker hypothesis</a>, proposed by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Damasio" title="Antonio Damasio">Antonio Damasio</a>, expands upon the James-Lange theory and posits that decisions and the ensuing behaviors are optimally guided by physiological patterns of interoceptive and emotional information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:15&#95;61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:15-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ensuing models focusing on the neurobiology of feelings states emphasized that the brain's mapping of different physiological body states are the critical ingredients for emotional experience and <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">consciousness</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In another model, <a href="/wiki/AD_(Bud)_Craig" class="mw-redirect" title="AD (Bud) Craig">Bud Craig</a> argues that the intertwining of interoceptive and homeostatic processes is responsible for initiating and maintaining motivational states and engendering human self-awareness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:10&#95;6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Interoception_and_illness">Interoception and illness</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Interoception and illness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Interoception_and_mental_illness">Interoception and mental illness</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Interoception and mental illness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Disturbances of interoception occur prominently and frequently in psychiatric disorders. These symptom fluctuations are often observed during the most severe expression of dysfunction, and they figure prominently in diagnostic classification of several psychiatric disorders. A few typical examples are reviewed next.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Panic_disorder">Panic disorder</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Panic disorder"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Palpitations" title="Palpitations">Palpitations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shortness_of_breath" title="Shortness of breath">dyspnea</a> are hallmarks of <a href="/wiki/Panic_attack" title="Panic attack">panic attacks</a>. Studies have shown that <a href="/wiki/Panic_disorder" title="Panic disorder">panic disorder</a> patients report a heightened experience of <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex#Interoceptive_awareness" title="Insular cortex">interoceptive sensations</a>, but these studies have failed to clarify whether this is simply due to their systematic bias toward describing such feelings.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, other studies have shown that panic disorder patients feel heartbeat sensations more intensely when the state of the body is perturbed by pharmacological agents, suggesting they exhibit heightened sensitivity to experiencing interoceptive sensations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Generalized_anxiety_disorder">Generalized anxiety disorder</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Generalized anxiety disorder"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Patients with <a href="/wiki/Generalized_anxiety_disorder" title="Generalized anxiety disorder">generalized anxiety disorder</a> (GAD) frequently report being bothered by interoceptive feelings of muscle tension, headaches, fatigue, gastrointestinal complaints, and pain.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Posttraumatic_stress_disorder">Posttraumatic stress disorder</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Posttraumatic stress disorder"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Functional_neuroimaging" title="Functional neuroimaging">Functional neuroimaging</a> studies have shown that <a href="/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">posttraumatic stress disorder</a> (PTSD) patients exhibit a decreased activation in the right anterior insula, a region of the brain that is largely responsible for identifying the mismatch between <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognitive</a> and interoceptive states.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:16&#95;68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:16-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Further, because PTSD patients have shown decreased activation within many nodes of the lamina I homeostatic pathway—a pathway through which the thalamus sends interoceptive information to the <a href="/wiki/Insular_cortex" title="Insular cortex">anterior insula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">anterior cingulate</a>—it has been suggested that PTSD patients experience reduced interoceptive awareness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:16&#95;68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:16-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Approaches such as <a href="/wiki/Somatic_experiencing" title="Somatic experiencing">somatic experiencing</a> use an interoceptive approach to treat PTSD.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Anxiety_disorders">Anxiety disorders</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Anxiety disorders"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The broad consensus of studies investigating the link between interoceptive awareness and anxiety disorders is that people with anxiety disorders experience heightened awareness of and accuracy in identifying interoceptive processes. Functional imaging studies provide evidence that people with anxiety disorders experience heightened interoceptive accuracy, suggested by hyperactivation in the <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">anterior cingulate cortex</a>—a region of the brain associated with interoception—in several different kinds of anxiety disorders.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The insula has been suggested to be abnormal in a large scale study across anxiety disorders in general.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other studies have found that interoceptive accuracy is increased in these patients, as evidenced by their superior ability in heartbeat detection tasks in comparison to healthy controls.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Anorexia_nervosa">Anorexia nervosa</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Anorexia nervosa"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Anorexia_nervosa" title="Anorexia nervosa">Anorexia nervosa</a> (AN) has been associated with interoceptive disturbances. Patients with AN often develop insensitivity to interoceptive cues of hunger, and yet are highly anxious and report disturbed interoceptive experiences, both inside and out.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While AN patients concentrate on distorted perceptions of their body exterior in fear of weight gain, they also report altered physical states <i>within</i> their bodies, such as indistinct feelings of fullness,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or an inability to distinguish emotional states from bodily sensations in general (called <a href="/wiki/Alexithymia" title="Alexithymia">alexithymia</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Bulimia_nervosa">Bulimia nervosa</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Bulimia nervosa"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Studies suggest that patients with and recovered from <a href="/wiki/Bulimia_nervosa" title="Bulimia nervosa">bulimia nervosa</a> (BN) exhibit abnormal interoceptive sensory processing<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and reduced interoceptive awareness under resting physiological conditions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Specifically, patients with BN report reduced sensitivity to many other kinds of internal and external sensations, exhibiting increased thresholds to heat pain compared to healthy subjects<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and an increased gastric capacity.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Neuroimaging literature suggests a pattern of abnormal interoceptive processing in patients with BN based on increased activity and volume in the insula and <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cingulate_cortex" title="Anterior cingulate cortex">anterior cingulate cortex</a>—regions associated with interoception and taste processing—when looking at food.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Major_depressive_disorder">Major depressive disorder</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Major depressive disorder"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">Major depressive disorder</a> (MDD) has been theoretically linked to interoceptive dysfunction. Studies have shown that women with MDD are less accurate on heartbeat counting tasks than are men with MDD<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and that, in general, patients with MDD are less accurate at counting heartbeat than are patients with panic or anxiety disorders.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, patients with MDD do not always exhibit reduced cardiac interoceptive accuracy; depressed patients experiencing high levels of anxiety will actually be more accurate on heartbeat detection tasks than depressed patients with lower levels of anxiety.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Somatic_symptom_disorders">Somatic symptom disorders</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Somatic symptom disorders"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Patients with <a href="/wiki/Somatic_symptom_disorder" title="Somatic symptom disorder">somatic symptom disorders</a> score lower on heartbeat detection tasks than healthy controls, suggesting that interoceptive accuracy is poor in psychosomatic disorders.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has also been found that patients with <a href="/wiki/Psychosomatic_medicine#Psychosomatic_disorders" title="Psychosomatic medicine">psychosomatic disorders</a> who are anxious or stressed report physical symptom discomfort at lower heart rates during exercise treadmill tests, implying poorer interoceptive <a href="/wiki/Distress_tolerance" title="Distress tolerance">distress tolerance</a> in somatic symptom disorders with comorbid psychiatric conditions.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Obsessive_compulsive_disorder">Obsessive compulsive disorder</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Obsessive compulsive disorder"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Results from a study investigating the relationship between obsessive compulsive disorder (OCD) and internal body signals found that patients with OCD were more accurate on a heartbeat perception task than healthy controls and anxiety patients heightened interoceptive awareness.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Autism_spectrum_disorder">Autism spectrum disorder</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Autism spectrum disorder"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Patients with <a href="/wiki/Autism_spectrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Autism spectrum">autism spectrum</a> disorder (ASD) may have poorer interoceptive awareness than control subjects. It is hypothesized that this decrease in interoceptive accuracy is due to <a href="/wiki/Alexithymia" title="Alexithymia">alexithymia</a>, which is often associated with ASD.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:17&#95;87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:17-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, it has also been found that children with ASD actually show greater interoceptive sensitivity than control subjects when measured over a long period of time.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:17&#95;87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:17-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Further investigation into the relationship between interoception and ASD is needed in order to fully understand the interoceptive aspect of the disorder.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Interoception_and_other_illness">Interoception and other illness</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Interoception and other illness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Fibromyalgia">Fibromyalgia</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Fibromyalgia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A 2024 study found that some <a href="/wiki/Fibromyalgia" title="Fibromyalgia">FM</a> people had higher interoception signals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Aphantasia">Aphantasia</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Aphantasia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Aphantasia—the absence of voluntary mental imagery—has been linked to disruptions in interoception, suggesting that vivid imagery relies on accurately sensing internal bodily states and exerting volitional control over them. According to the interoceptive theory of mental imagery and aphantasia, Interoception may provide the embodied grounding necessary for generating and consciously controlling mental simulations.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Current_theories_of_interoceptive_processing">Current theories of interoceptive processing</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Current theories of interoceptive processing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Predictive_coding#Interoception" title="Predictive coding">Predictive coding §&#160;Interoception</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Embodied_predictive_interoception_coding_(EPIC)"><span id="Embodied_predictive_interoception_coding_.28EPIC.29"></span>Embodied predictive interoception coding (EPIC)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Embodied predictive interoception coding (EPIC)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The EPIC model proposes a method of understanding the brain's response to stimuli contrary to the classic "stimulus-response" model. The classical view of information processing is that when a peripheral stimulus provided information to the <a href="/wiki/Central_nervous_system" title="Central nervous system">central nervous system</a>, it was processed in the brain, and a response was elicited. The EPIC model<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:12&#95;5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> deviates from this and proposes that the brain is involved in a process of <a href="/wiki/Free_energy_principle#Active_inference" title="Free energy principle">active inference</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that is, assiduously making predictions about situations based on previous experiences. These predictions, when coupled with incoming sensory signals, allow the brain to compute a prediction error. Interoceptive prediction errors signal the occurrence of discrepancies within the body, which the brain attempts to minimize. This can be done by modifying the predictions through brain-related pathways, altering the body position/location in order to better align incoming sensory signals with the prediction, or altering the brain's method of receiving incoming stimuli.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:12&#95;5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Interoceptive prediction error signals are a key component of many theories of interoceptive dysfunction in physical and mental health.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Research_and_treatments">Research and treatments</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Research and treatments"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Float_tank.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Float_tank.png/250px-Float_tank.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Float_tank.png 1.5x" data-file-width="496" data-file-height="329" /></a><figcaption>An open float pool</figcaption></figure>
<p>As attention on interoception increases among the scientific community, new research methods and treatment tactics are beginning to emerge. Because there currently is not a clear consensus as to what exactly interoception is, or the best ways in which to measure it, most research and questionnaires on the subject only measure individual facets of interoception. The convergence and interrelatedness of the questionnaire items between the constructs has been found to be low.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Ongoing research in interoception has shown the importance of perturbing interoceptive systems.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This allows researchers the ability to document the effects of non-baseline states, which occur during times of panic or anxiety. It also provides the participant the ability to gauge the intensity of sensations within the body. This can be done through pharmacological interventions, balloon distensions, or respiratory breathing loads depending on the interoceptive system of interest.
</p><p>Another research method used to study interoception is specialized <a href="/wiki/Isolation_tank" title="Isolation tank">flotation environments</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:18&#95;96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:18-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Floating removes external stimuli so that individuals can more easily focus on the interoceptive sensations within their bodies. One idea with floating is that over many float sessions, patients with different kinds of disorders may learn to become more attuned or tolerant of their interoceptive sensations not only in the <a href="/wiki/Isolation_tank" title="Isolation tank">float tank</a> but also in their everyday lives.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:18&#95;96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:18-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Whole body <a href="/wiki/Hyperthermia" title="Hyperthermia">hyperthermia</a> may provide a new treatment technique for <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is thought that reducing one of the bodily symptoms of depression, which is increased <a href="/wiki/Inflammation" title="Inflammation">inflammation</a>, using whole body hyperthermia will also reduce depressive feelings represented in the brain. In theory, these techniques will help patients better attune themselves to their interoceptive sensations, allowing them a better understanding of what occurs in their bodies.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Acupuncture" title="Acupuncture">Acupuncture</a> is an alternative treatment type for many people with anxiety and depression. Typically, it is self-prescribed by patients;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> however, results are inconclusive on its ability to manage symptoms of <a href="/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">depression</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Recently, <a href="/wiki/Massage" title="Massage">Massage</a> therapy has been shown to have the ability to reduce symptoms of generalized anxiety disorder.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Meditation" title="Meditation">Meditation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mindfulness-based_cognitive_therapy" title="Mindfulness-based cognitive therapy">mindfulness</a> have been looked into as possible techniques to enhance interoceptive awareness based on their tendency to redirect focus within oneself. Studies show that meditation and mindfulness practices promote attention to interoceptive sensations. In reality, with all the benefits of mindfulness, many may be ascribed to an increase in interoception.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, interoceptive awareness and accuracy in specific domains such as breath or body monitoring, may be more independent from a broad improvement in interoceptive accuracy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Meditation and mindfulness practices have been shown to modify the insula, which is considered central to our interoceptive abilities.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-:19&#95;37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:19-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Attention is also being given to the <a href="/wiki/Subtle_body" title="Subtle body">subtle body</a> and its function as a CNS map in traditional Tibetan and Indian medicine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although a universal definition of interoception has not been reached, research on interoception and <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">psychiatric disorders</a> has shown a link between interoceptive processing and mental disorders. It has been proposed that <a href="/wiki/Exposure_therapy" title="Exposure therapy">exposure therapy</a>, a commonly employed treatment for <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">anxiety disorders</a>, may provide a basis for a model of <a href="/wiki/Interoceptive_exposure" title="Interoceptive exposure">interoceptive exposure</a> therapy that could be incorporated into treatment plans of different psychiatric disorders.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One proposal states that multiple interoceptive challenges assessing different physiological systems could provide diagnosticians with the ability to create an "interoceptive profile" for a specific individual, creating a patient-specific treatment plan.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:3&#95;2-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interoception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: See also"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Inflammatory_reflex" title="Inflammatory reflex">Inflammatory reflex</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Proprioception" title="Proprioception">Proprioception</a></li></ul>

</li>
<li id="cite&#95;note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1333433106" /><cite id="CITEREFFoxCahn2018" class="citation book cs1">Fox, Kieran; Cahn, B.
